## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: The task belongs to population ecology, where the growth rate dP/dt is modeled as a function of current population P and time t. The goal is to discover differential equation structures commonly used to describe exponential, logistic, density-dependent, Allee effect, and time-varying growth phenomena.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per capita growth rate)
- Logistic growth (quadratic): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (where c1 is negative, representing intraspecific competition)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (or c0*P*log(c1/P), sigmoidal with asymmetric growth)
- Allee effect (cubic): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (low-density positive feedback and high-density competition)
- Generalized logistic (power-density): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (density-dependent mortality with adjustable exponent)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (balance between anabolic surface-limited growth and catabolic mass-proportional loss)
- Harvested logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (constant yield harvesting)
- Saturating per capita growth: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (Type II functional response limiting growth rate)
- Seasonal forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * sin(c2 * t) * P (periodic environmental effects on growth rate)
- Time-decaying growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changes exponentially with time, e.g., resource depletion)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * t**c1 (time-dependent immigration or environmental forcing)
- Hyperbolic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 / (1 + c1 * P) (growth rate decreases hyperbolically with population size)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear P term alone → exponential growth behavior, indicating unlimited resources
- Negative quadratic P**2 term → logistic density dependence, intraspecific competition
- Cubic P**3 term → Allee effect, where growth is reduced or negative at very low densities
- Logarithm of P, like P*log(K/P) → Gompertz curve, asymmetric S-shaped growth often in tumors or aging populations
- Power exponent in P (P**c with c not 1 or 2) → allometric scaling, e.g., metabolic growth limitation
- Constant term without P → constant immigration or harvesting independent of current population
- Sine/cosine of time → seasonal or diurnal forcing in population growth
- Rational form P/(1+P) → saturating per capita growth, typical of predator saturation or resource limitation
